FoREwoRd By ThE EXECuTiVE  diRECT oR | 7

--- Document Chunk 288 ---
Foreword by the 

--- Document Chunk 289 ---
Executive director

--- Document Chunk 290 ---
“A sustainable, safe European transport system without frontiers ” not only repre-

--- Document Chunk 291 ---
sents our Agency’s vision, but also reflects the unprecedented challenges that transport 

--- Document Chunk 292 ---
in Europe is facing in the general pursuit of the green mobility goals, while also taking into 

--- Document Chunk 293 ---
account the consequences of the CoVid-19 pandemic. in a world that faces a resurgence 

--- Document Chunk 294 ---
of violence and war, we witness every day the strategic importance of railways. The trans-

--- Document Chunk 295 ---
port of critical supplies and of people to safety through railways in ukraine is a testimony 

--- Document Chunk 296 ---
to the vital importance of rail. 

--- Document Chunk 297 ---
in line with its mandate, the European union Agency for Railways aims at covering a wide 

--- Document Chunk 298 ---
range of areas of work, involving actions to drive the continuation of the progress with 

--- Document Chunk 299 ---
railway safety and interoperability, together with its role of Eu-wide authority for Vehicle 

--- Document Chunk 300 ---
Authorisation, single safety Certification, and ERTMs Trackside Approval.

--- Document Chunk 301 ---
The multi-annual work programme 2023-2025, together with the annual programme 

--- Document Chunk 302 ---
2023 have been planned and drafted following the intervention logic  principles, on 

--- Document Chunk 303 ---
the basis of the conclusions of the sPd 2023 workshop held with the Management Board 

--- Document Chunk 304 ---
in July 2021. since 2022, the Agency’s work has been organised around the agreed set of 

--- Document Chunk 305 ---
seven strategic statements , which projects the Agency’s role in relation to its stake -

--- Document Chunk 306 ---
holders, complemented by two transversal strategic statements , which capture the 

--- Document Chunk 307 ---
Agency’s governance and support functions. 

--- Document Chunk 308 ---
in the third year after the transposition by all Member states of the 4th Railway Package 

--- Document Chunk 309 ---
technical pillar, the Agency has gained significant experience in running the tasks re -

--- Document Chunk 310 ---
lated to the Authority role, as well as in forecasting their volume to the best extent possi -

--- Document Chunk 311 ---
ble. indeed, based on an analysis carried out on previous years’ patterns, the Agency can 

--- Document Chunk 312 ---
identify more accurately peak periods for the expected submission of applications, which 

--- Document Chunk 313 ---
are now reflected in its planning. i n addition, the Agency has reached a higher maturity 

--- Document Chunk 314 ---
level with the processing of authorisation and certification tasks, which has a potential for 

--- Document Chunk 315 ---
driving a higher efficiency in their delivery. 

--- Document Chunk 316 ---
while the level of ambition and action for the Agency around the defined strategic state-

--- Document Chunk 317 ---
ments can be very high, as also confirmed by the Management Board expectations during 

--- Document Chunk 318 ---
the sPd 2023 workshop, the Agency has put in place a stronger mechanism of internal ar-

--- Document Chunk 319 ---
bitration in order to identify priorities and put forward the expected outputs, which can fit 

--- Document Chunk 320 ---
within the available envelope of budget and human resources in order to ensure the best 

--- Document Chunk 321 ---
value for money for the Eu citizens. while the Agency’s ambition is to affirm its increasingly 

--- Document Chunk 322 ---
stronger position as the technical reference for the progress with railway interoperability 

--- Document Chunk 323 ---
and safety in the Eu, it had been faced with the challenge of deploying a too limited num-

--- Document Chunk 324 ---
ber of posts as compared to its needs to cope with the simultaneous pressure from the 

--- Document Chunk 325 ---
policy and the authority tasks. 

--- Document Chunk 326 ---
in 2022, the Agency’s Management Board adopted the Strengthening Plan prepared 

--- Document Chunk 327 ---
by the Agency in close cooperation with the European Commission. with the document 

--- Document Chunk 328 ---
serving as a basis for the internal EC budget negotiations in 2022, the Agency received a 

--- Document Chunk 329 ---
proposed increase of 12 temporary agent posts (TAs) starting 2023. while the additional 

--- Document Chunk 330 ---
TA allocation is lower compared to the request from the strengthening Plan (12 TAs pro -

--- Document Chunk 331 ---
posed out of the 22 TAs requested), it can offer a good basis for the Agency to proceed 

--- Document Chunk 332 ---
with the implementation of the strengthening Plan. A very important challenge is repre -

--- Document Chunk 333 ---
sented by the fact that the additional TA allocation needs to be fully covered under the 

--- Document Chunk 334 ---
existing budget envelope. To make best use of this TA allocation and considering the very 

--- Document Chunk 335 ---
Josef Doppelbauer

--- Document Chunk 336 ---
Foreword by the Executive director

--- Document Chunk 337 ---
8 | singLE PR ogRAMMing  doCuMEnT 2023-2025

--- Document Chunk 338 ---
likely high budget pressure related to the indexation of salaries and prices, the Agency is 

--- Document Chunk 339 ---
making a thorough assessment of its capacity to cover these costs in a sustainable manner 

--- Document Chunk 340 ---
until the end of MFF 2021-2027. several measures are envisaged, such as the time-phased 

--- Document Chunk 341 ---
hiring of the TAs. The budget constraint on the subsidy side is an element to be properly 

--- Document Chunk 342 ---
monitored and managed for the remaining period of the current MFF, especially in the 

--- Document Chunk 343 ---
context of the very challenging and volatile context of salary and price indexation, started 

--- Document Chunk 344 ---
in 2022. The sPd 2023 displays the assignment of these additional posts to the priority 

--- Document Chunk 345 ---
areas identified in the strengthening Plan and factors a prudent approach by means of 

--- Document Chunk 346 ---
a correction coefficient for late hiring during the year. Additionally,  the Agency is making 

--- Document Chunk 347 ---
sustained efforts for a combined response to the resourcing challenge by increasing the 

--- Document Chunk 348 ---
direct utilisation of its resources, both in terms of budget and FTEs.

--- Document Chunk 349 ---
The Agency keeps a strong commitment to deploying the necessary resources for meet-

--- Document Chunk 350 ---
ing the legal deadlines for the issuing of VA, ssC and ERTMs Trackside approvals, while also 

--- Document Chunk 351 ---
respecting the deadlines for its safety and interoperability related activities, all of which 

--- Document Chunk 352 ---
contribute to the achievement of the high-level policy objectives of the 4 th Railway Pack-

--- Document Chunk 353 ---
age. The decision time linked to the authority tasks has undeniably a tremendous impact 

--- Document Chunk 354 ---
on the rail stakeholders and on the competitiveness of rail compared with other sectors. 

--- Document Chunk 355 ---
The Agency would also like to bring forward interesting and new projects  that could 

--- Document Chunk 356 ---
benefit the entire rail sector. we would like to develop a new safety information sharing 

--- Document Chunk 357 ---
tool in the context of the CsM on the assessment of safety Levels and safety Performance, 

--- Document Chunk 358 ---
including occurrence reporting. This activity will involve a budgetary need to build the 

--- Document Chunk 359 ---
tool, as well as an ongoing resource need to run the tool, to perform an analysis and 

--- Document Chunk 360 ---
generate learning at European level, which is the ultimate added value. This task is a clear 

--- Document Chunk 361 ---
example of a new legal obligation for which the Agency would need to receive an addi -

--- Document Chunk 362 ---
tional dedicated budget envelope.

--- Document Chunk 363 ---
i would like to assure the members of the Management Board that the Agency will con -

--- Document Chunk 364 ---

Mission sTATEMEnT  | 9

--- Document Chunk 388 ---
Mission statement

--- Document Chunk 389 ---
The updated vision and mission statements of the Agency (“A sustainable, safe European 

--- Document Chunk 390 ---
transport system without frontiers” and “Moving Europe towards a sustainable and safe 

--- Document Chunk 391 ---
railway system without frontiers” , respectively) were defined in 2021, following intense 

--- Document Chunk 392 ---
work carried out through the organisational culture change (Better Together) project, with 

--- Document Chunk 393 ---
the explicit aim to have full staff buy-in. The new mission and vision statements of the 

--- Document Chunk 394 ---
Agency better reflect its current position and role, while of course remaining fully in line 

--- Document Chunk 395 ---
with the legal mandate of the Agency. 

--- Document Chunk 396 ---
The Agency contributes to the further development and effective functioning of a single 

--- Document Chunk 397 ---
European Railway Area without frontiers, by guaranteeing a high level of railway safety 

--- Document Chunk 398 ---
and interoperability, while improving the competitive position of the railway sector, as 

--- Document Chunk 399 ---
envisaged by the Agency Regulation 2016/796. in particular, the Agency shall contribute, 

--- Document Chunk 400 ---
on technical matters, to the implementation of union legislation by developing a com -

--- Document Chunk 401 ---
mon approach to safety on the union rail system and by enhancing the level of interoper-

--- Document Chunk 402 ---
ability on the union rail system and associated data, with a specific focus on facilitating the 

--- Document Chunk 403 ---
interoperable deployment of ERTMs and on access to data for pushing rail modernisation 

--- Document Chunk 404 ---
and digitalisation. By working in close cooperation with the national authorities acting in 

--- Document Chunk 405 ---
the fields of railway safety and interoperability, the Agency will substantially contribute 

--- Document Chunk 406 ---
to an increased competitiveness of rail and to the seamless cross-border traffic in the Eu . 

--- Document Chunk 407 ---
Moreover, through timely delivery of appropriate regulation that reflects the harmonised 

--- Document Chunk 408 ---
and validated solution proposals from the Europe’s Rail Joint undertaking, the Agency 

--- Document Chunk 409 ---
contributes significantly to the coordinated and rapid deployment of such solutions, thus 

--- Document Chunk 410 ---
strengthening the competitiveness of rail in the transport mix. All these elements are 

--- Document Chunk 411 ---
translated into rail becoming more attractive and affordable for passengers and freight, 

--- Document Chunk 412 ---
with the Agency playing an active role in supporting the delivery of the European green 

--- Document Chunk 413 ---
deal for the Eu citizens and businesses.

gEnERAL  ConTEXT  | 13

--- Document Chunk 581 ---
i. general context

--- Document Chunk 582 ---
14 | singLE PR ogRAMMing  doCuMEnT 2023-2025

--- Document Chunk 583 ---
Transport is an essential part of the European integration, especially given its contribution 

--- Document Chunk 584 ---
to the functioning of the free movement of services, goods, and people. Transport also 

--- Document Chunk 585 ---
represents around 5% of the Eu gdP and directly employs around 10 million workers( 1), 

--- Document Chunk 586 ---
therefore representing an important sector for society at large. Eu transport policies have 

--- Document Chunk 587 ---
been developed according to the key principles of safety, sustainability, resilience, connec-

--- Document Chunk 588 ---
tivity, and efficiency.

--- Document Chunk 589 ---
Through its long-term vision for the transport sector and European society, the European 

--- Document Chunk 590 ---
Commission published in 2020 the Sustainable and Smart Mobility Strategy with a detailed 

--- Document Chunk 591 ---
action plan of 82 initiatives. with this strategy, the Commission presents how the Eu trans-

--- Document Chunk 592 ---
port system will achieve its needed green and digital transformation and become more 

--- Document Chunk 593 ---
resilient. As outlined in the European green d eal, the result will be a 90% cut in carbon 

--- Document Chunk 594 ---
emissions by 2050. Regarding the rail sector, the following targets have been set:

--- Document Chunk 595 ---
  Traffic on high-speed rail will double by 2030

--- Document Chunk 596 ---
  Rail freight traffic will increase by 50% by 2030 and double by 2050

--- Document Chunk 597 ---
  By 2030, rail and waterborne-based intermodal transport will be able to compete 

--- Document Chunk 598 ---
on equal footing with road-only transport in the Eu

--- Document Chunk 599 ---
The European union Agency for Railways will support the European Commission, in line 

--- Document Chunk 600 ---
with its accountability ceiling, in achieving these goals, in particular through the further 

--- Document Chunk 601 ---
development and effective functioning of a single European Railway Area without fron -

--- Document Chunk 602 ---
tiers.

--- Document Chunk 603 ---
The 2023-2025 programming period for the Agency involves two different types of activ-

--- Document Chunk 604 ---
ities: 

--- Document Chunk 605 ---
  The policy tasks contributing to the implementation of union legislation by de -

--- Document Chunk 606 ---
veloping a common approach to safety on the union rail system and by enhanc -

--- Document Chunk 607 ---
ing the level of interoperability on the union rail system, taking into account the 

--- Document Chunk 608 ---
policy priorities identified in the strengthening Plan 2023-2027, as endorsed by 

--- Document Chunk 609 ---
the Agency’s Management Board in 2022.

--- Document Chunk 610 ---
  The full-fledged performance of the Agency’s tasks as Eu-wide authority for 

--- Document Chunk 611 ---
safety certification, vehicle authorisation and ERTMs trackside approval, along with 

--- Document Chunk 612 ---
other tasks in the field of railway safety and interoperability as foreseen in the Tech-

--- Document Chunk 613 ---
nical Pillar of the Fourth Railway Package.

--- Document Chunk 614 ---
The Agency has been implementing an innovative structure to its work programme, which 

--- Document Chunk 615 ---
responds to the intervention logic requirements, in line with the guidelines provided by 

--- Document Chunk 616 ---
the network of Eu Agencies. i t also strives to increase its efficiency in delivering the out -

--- Document Chunk 617 ---
comes and impacts expected by Eu citizens. in light of the above, the work programme of 

--- Document Chunk 618 ---
the Agency (in its multi-annual and annual planning) is organised around seven strategic 

--- Document Chunk 619 ---
statements, which project the Agency’s role in relation to its stakeholders, complement -

--- Document Chunk 620 ---
ed by two transversal strategic statements, which capture the Agency’s governance and 

--- Document Chunk 621 ---
support functions. These strategic statements were adopted by the MB for sPd 2022-2024 

--- Document Chunk 622 ---
and are extremely important, as they show the direction of travel on which the Agency 

--- Document Chunk 623 ---
plans to embark in order to make railways work better for society, subject to its remit and 

--- Document Chunk 624 ---
accountability ceiling. The concrete Agency work, represented by projects and services 

--- Document Chunk 625 ---
with concrete outputs, is organised by grouping the projects and services which together 

--- Document Chunk 626 ---
can contribute to the outcomes and impacts stated in a particular strategic statement. 

--- Document Chunk 627 ---
in sPd 2023, the Agency has further implemented the intervention logic. while for the 

--- Document Chunk 628 ---
previous years the multiannual section was presented mainly with overarching objectives 

--- Document Chunk 629 ---
to achieve, the planning will now include more detailed FTEs and budget figures. This 

--- Document Chunk 630 ---
additional level of granularity will provide more reliable data to monitor and a coherent 

--- Document Chunk 631 ---
stability for the Agency. of course, the Agency will remain flexible and redeploy resources 

--- Document Chunk 632 ---
(1)  https://ec.europa.eu/commission/presscorner/detail/en/fs_20_2350

if needed, but the new approach provides a roadmap for all stakeholders regarding the

--- Document Chunk 810 ---

--- Document Chunk 812 ---

tem’s resilience to interoperability issues and increase cross-border traffic.

Multi-annual programming 2023-2025

--- Document Chunk 892 ---
The Agency is playing a pivotal role in supporting the transformation of the European 

--- Document Chunk 893 ---
transport system towards decarbonised, interoperable and safe transport modes based 

--- Document Chunk 894 ---
on multi-modal integration (Maas). 

--- Document Chunk 895 ---
in 2022, the Agency provided substantial inputs to the green deal deliverables and played 

--- Document Chunk 896 ---
a key role for driving the data and digitalisation agenda for railways, based on the linked 

--- Document Chunk 897 ---
data pilots and the revision of TAP/TAF T si. Those elements are particularly relevant in a 

--- Document Chunk 898 ---
multi-modal context as they enable that integration in terms of ticketing and timetables 

--- Document Chunk 899 ---
which has been preventing the effective development of rail as the backbone of a mul -

--- Document Chunk 900 ---
ti-modal and international transport.

--- Document Chunk 901 ---
The Agency has identified for this strategic statement two intermediate outcomes, which 

--- Document Chunk 902 ---
will support the achievement of the overarching statement. There are the following ones:

--- Document Chunk 903 ---
1. TAP is implemented by all relevant railway actors (iMs, Rus, ticket vendors), it is ac -

--- Document Chunk 904 ---
tually used as the main channel of information exchange and the ticketing is inte-

--- Document Chunk 905 ---
grated in the multimodal environment with other transport modes

--- Document Chunk 906 ---
2. TAF is implemented by all relevant railway actors (iMs, Rus, wKs, CTos) and it is actu-

--- Document Chunk 907 ---
ally used as the main channel of information exchange

--- Document Chunk 908 ---
of course, TAF and TAP Tsi will also be in scope for some intermediate outcomes already 

--- Document Chunk 909 ---
identified under strategic statement 1. Additional intermediate outcomes will be identi -

--- Document Chunk 910 ---
fied in the future to further implement the intervention logic within the Agency. 

--- Document Chunk 911 ---
For the period 2023-2025, the Agency will still be a top player in ensuring the right frame-

--- Document Chunk 912 ---
work for the data and information exchange related to assets and services (includ-

--- Document Chunk 913 ---
ing ticketing data), based on linked data, universal data identifiers and more and better 

--- Document Chunk 914 ---
data exchanged between operators and customers. This will ensure a seamless exchange 

--- Document Chunk 915 ---
of data with other modes of transport, thus allowing the customers to benefit from a 

--- Document Chunk 916 ---
comprehensive logistics chain or the mobility-as-a-service, respectively. i n addition, the 

--- Document Chunk 917 ---
Agency has triggered its path to convert the Eu Railway Registers in building blocks within 

--- Document Chunk 918 ---
the European Common Mobility data space (item 71). i n 2020-2022, the Agency trans -

--- Document Chunk 919 ---
formed and linked together the Register of Eu railway infrastructure (RinF) dataset and 

--- Document Chunk 920 ---
the European Type of Vehicle (ERATV partly) dataset into a Knowledge graph (~26 million 

--- Document Chunk 921 ---
triples), making this data interoperable, findable, and providing semantically enriched 

--- Document Chunk 922 ---
machine and human query services. The Agency has followed the directive 2019/1024 on 

--- Document Chunk 923 ---
open data, the Eu data strategy, the data Act -FAiR principles, the principle of technology 

--- Document Chunk 924 ---
neutrality- and the Eu policy on reference data. Moreover, the Agency is a publisher in the 

--- Document Chunk 925 ---
open data portal, with 13 datasets published. The data and digitalization roadmap 2021-

--- Document Chunk 926 ---
2024 proposes to add gradually new datasets (in-house data) to this knowledge graph 

--- Document Chunk 927 ---
as well as links to external datasets to facilitate multimodal data exchange. Currently, the 

--- Document Chunk 928 ---
Agency is developing the strategic direction for linked data in relation to RinF under stra-

--- Document Chunk 929 ---
tegic statement 8, while exploring the mainstreaming of this approach to other registers 

--- Document Chunk 930 ---
and databases. once moved from a strategic development concept to a mainstreamed 

--- Document Chunk 931 ---
approach, this stream of work will be covered under strategic statement 2 and 3. i n addi-

--- Document Chunk 932 ---
tion, the TAF TSI will provide the data communication requirements for the transparent 

--- Document Chunk 933 ---
and efficient traffic management and train operations system of the future including also 

--- Document Chunk 934 ---
(i) first and last mile logistic segments involving intermodal actors (operators, terminals) 

--- Document Chunk 935 ---
and (ii) linkage to other modes of transport (road, waterborne). This will also contain the 

--- Document Chunk 936 ---
enhanced simple and smart tracking of trains, wagons and consignments. The same T si 

--- Document Chunk 937 ---
will also include additional requirements for the setting up of Laas starting from consign-

--- Document Chunk 938 ---
ment order (intermodal compliant), train operation preparation and ending in well-pre -

--- Document Chunk 939 ---
dicted / efficient delivery of trains, wagons and consignments to the business partners.

--- Document Chunk 940 ---
Concerning the environmental sustainability of the railway system, the Agency will con -

--- Document Chunk 941 ---
tinue to deliver support and assistance to the EC for the Green Deal, as well as for the co-

--- Document Chunk 942 ---
ordination of transport of dangerous goods by rail, recognising that in many cases 

--- Document Chunk 943 ---
the Commission has the lead role.

--- Document Chunk 979 ---
in the field of Railway safety, the Agency has identified 3 categories of intermediate out -

--- Document Chunk 980 ---
comes that it can actively influence through its portfolio of safety related projects and 

--- Document Chunk 981 ---
services and that are essential pre-conditions to achieve the strategic statement 4. The 

--- Document Chunk 982 ---
identified intermediate outcomes are as follows:

--- Document Chunk 983 ---

--- Document Chunk 984 ---
actively implement an sMs to control the risks of operational activities;

--- Document Chunk 985 ---

--- Document Chunk 986 ---
the system - ERA, Ms, nsA, AsBo, ECM CB, accreditation, recognition, niB;

--- Document Chunk 987 ---
3. safety and safety management/performance related data is shared in an open and 

--- Document Chunk 988 ---
transparent way;

--- Document Chunk 989 ---
The Agency can influence the positive progress towards the achievement of these out -

--- Document Chunk 990 ---
comes by intervening in the following 5 ways:

--- Document Chunk 991 ---
  Building knowledge: to build ERA/sector knowledge on how to achieve the de-

--- Document Chunk 992 ---
sired outcome;

--- Document Chunk 993 ---
  Regulating: providing the input to regulate via Eu legislation the desired out -

--- Document Chunk 994 ---
comes;

--- Document Chunk 995 ---

--- Document Chunk 996 ---
comes;

--- Document Chunk 997 ---
  Monitoring: to monitor the actual status of achieving the desired outcomes and 

--- Document Chunk 998 ---
understanding the difficulties the sector is encountering;

--- Document Chunk 999 ---
  Reinforcing: to enforce/reinforce the actual status of achieving the desired out -

--- Document Chunk 1000 ---
comes.

--- Document Chunk 1001 ---
up until now the Agency has invested most of its efforts in building knowledge and pro -

--- Document Chunk 1002 ---
viding the input for regulating, while not sufficiently supporting the railway sector in the 

--- Document Chunk 1003 ---

comes and interventions for statement 4 the Agency will continue to focus on:

lation and strengthening nsAs’ and niBs’ capacity, in line with principles and legal

approach, partly through SSC applications. (sharing knowledge/ monitoring/

  The continuous cooperation of the Agency with the EuAn network, as well as the 

--- Document Chunk 1449 ---
European Commission to increase its efficiency, including shared services or the 

--- Document Chunk 1450 ---
migration to suMMA in 2022 as one of the three pilot agencies.

--- Document Chunk 1451 ---
  The new prioritisation exercise (arbitration), focusing on multiannual planning, 

--- Document Chunk 1452 ---
and allocating resources in the most efficient manner, based on the highest value 

--- Document Chunk 1453 ---
for money for the Eu citizens.

--- Document Chunk 1454 ---
  Following a high number of valuable ad-hoc exchanges of expertise between 

--- Document Chunk 1455 ---
EAsA and ERA, the Agency has initiated the formalisation of the Cooperation with 

--- Document Chunk 1456 ---
EAsA and has defined the initial core areas of cooperation.

--- Document Chunk 1457 ---
while the Agency will continue to strive for an even higher efficiency all across its process-

--- Document Chunk 1458 ---
es and activities, its ambition is to affirm its stronger and stronger position as the technical 

--- Document Chunk 1459 ---
reference for the progress with railway interoperability and safety in the Eu . The Agen -

--- Document Chunk 1460 ---
cy worked, in close cooperation with the European Commission, to put forward a com -

--- Document Chunk 1461 ---
prehensive strengthening plan, which has been endorsed by the Management Board in 

--- Document Chunk 1462 ---
2022. its main objective is to ensure that the Agency has the right level of resources 

--- Document Chunk 1463 ---
to perform the most adding value activities in an effective and efficient manner, 

--- Document Chunk 1464 ---
in line with its ambition level. 

--- Document Chunk 1465 ---
The Strengthening plan is built on the following pillars:

--- Document Chunk 1466 ---
1. Further consolidating the data collection and transparency through reinforced 

--- Document Chunk 1467 ---
monitoring and a data-driven performance culture. This will entail the use and 

--- Document Chunk 1468 ---
further improvement of the existing tools and mechanism which yielded results 

--- Document Chunk 1469 ---
starting 2021, such as the sPd dashboard.

--- Document Chunk 1470 ---
2. Budget planning, management, and absorption leading to better budget execu -

--- Document Chunk 1471 ---
tion. This will entail the use and further improvement of the existing tools and 

--- Document Chunk 1472 ---
mechanism which already yielded results in 2021, such as the budget execution 

--- Document Chunk 1473 ---
monitoring. For the items of expenditure which represent a significant share of the 

--- Document Chunk 1474 ---
Agency’s budget, benchmarking analyses with similar organisations will be run 

--- Document Chunk 1475 ---
and opportunities to use shared services with other agencies or with the EC will 

--- Document Chunk 1476 ---
be analysed.

--- Document Chunk 1477 ---
3. higher administrative efficiency: the Agency will further increase the direct utili -

--- Document Chunk 1478 ---
sation of all its resources, will continue to seek for process efficiencies, including 

--- Document Chunk 1479 ---
through digitalisation and automation and will look at the most effective solutions 

--- Document Chunk 1480 ---
for sub-contracting non-critical and non-sensitive pieces of work.

--- Document Chunk 1481 ---
4. Targeting the resources to achieve the Eu policy objectives. while the level of am -

--- Document Chunk 1482 ---
bition and action for the Agency around the defined strategic statements can be 

--- Document Chunk 1483 ---
very high, as also confirmed by the MB expectations during the sPd 2023 work -

--- Document Chunk 1484 ---
shop, the Agency has put in place a mechanism of internal arbitration in order to 

--- Document Chunk 1485 ---
identify and put forward the priorities which can fit within the available envelope 

--- Document Chunk 1486 ---
of budget and human resources in order to ensure the best value for money for 

--- Document Chunk 1487 ---
the Eu citizens.

--- Document Chunk 1488 ---
5. Predictability and sustainability of Authority work: the Agency is continuously im -

--- Document Chunk 1489 ---
proving the predictability of its authority tasks volume of work, while also working 

--- Document Chunk 1490 ---
on the streamlining of processes, including through automation (e.g. for the con -

--- Document Chunk 1491 ---
formity to type activities) and better training of applicants.

--- Document Chunk 1492 ---
The strengthening Plan Task Force has been set up within the Agency and it will submit its 

--- Document Chunk 1493 ---
Action Plan 2023-2027 to the MB in november 2022.

  ERA Academy

--- Document Chunk 1506 ---

--- Document Chunk 1507 ---

--- Document Chunk 1508 ---
al 12 FTEs granted to the Agency. This might result in longer time to implement 

--- Document Chunk 1509 ---

--- Document Chunk 1510 ---

--- Document Chunk 1511 ---
stakeholders as essential to improve Railway safety.

--- Document Chunk 1512 ---
  Common Safety Methods on Assessment of Safety Level and Safety Performance

--- Document Chunk 1513 ---
The CMs AsLP project and its future success heavily depend on the development 

--- Document Chunk 1514 ---
of the information sharing system (iss). it could be adapted from ECCAiRs2, which 

--- Document Chunk 1515 ---
is a digital platform managed by the European Aviation safety Agency assisting 

--- Document Chunk 1516 ---
aviation stakeholders in collecting, sharing, and analysing safety aviation informa -

--- Document Chunk 1517 ---
tion. The benefits of adapting this platform to rails could be quite important and 

--- Document Chunk 1518 ---
the Agency would need a sufficient budget to ensure its complete implementa -

--- Document Chunk 1519 ---
tion. depending on the complexity of the options selected for adapting ECCAiRs2, 

--- Document Chunk 1520 ---
costs could range from 900k € to over 3 million €. with the current budget en -

--- Document Chunk 1521 ---
velope, this need cannot be covered. The Agency is further assessing the possi -

--- Document Chunk 1522 ---
ble options and will exchange on this additional budget need with the European 

--- Document Chunk 1523 ---
Commission.

--- Document Chunk 1528 ---
Annual work programme 2023

--- Document Chunk 1529 ---
Executive summary

--- Document Chunk 1530 ---
The Annual work Programme for 2023 details all the projects and services which will be 

--- Document Chunk 1531 ---
carried out to contribute to the Agency’s goals in the year. The structure of the work Pro-

--- Document Chunk 1532 ---
gramme has been redesigned in order to organise the work of the Agency against desired 

--- Document Chunk 1533 ---
long-term outcomes, implementing therefore an effective multi-annual work programme 

--- Document Chunk 1534 ---
with developed objectives, as well as the intervention logic. 

--- Document Chunk 1535 ---
The annual work programme 2023 had been aligned to the priorities listed in the Agency’s 

--- Document Chunk 1536 ---
strengthening Plan and the corresponding implementing document (sAP 2023-2027), 

--- Document Chunk 1537 ---
which represents an anchor for the planning in sPd 2023 and the subsequent ones. 

--- Document Chunk 1538 ---
The Agency’s efforts in 2023 are particularly focused on:

--- Document Chunk 1539 ---
  Technical and operational barriers: The Agency will work towards the reduc -

--- Document Chunk 1540 ---
tion of technical and operations barriers within the rail market through, among 

--- Document Chunk 1541 ---
others, the amendment of T sis to be aligned with the technical innovations, har -

--- Document Chunk 1542 ---
monisation of national rules among Mss, continuous noBo monitoring, the deliv -

--- Document Chunk 1543 ---
ery of 4th Railway package activities (ssC, ERTMs TA, VA), and the deployment of 

--- Document Chunk 1544 ---
ERTMs. 

--- Document Chunk 1545 ---
  Safety: The Agency will strengthen safety on rail through the development of 

--- Document Chunk 1546 ---
a safety culture, the monitoring of national safety Authority, the Common safe -

--- Document Chunk 1547 ---
ty Methods on Assessment of safety Level and safety Performance (within the 

--- Document Chunk 1548 ---
boundaries linked to the resource constraints for the information sharing system), 

--- Document Chunk 1549 ---
and other relevant projects. 

--- Document Chunk 1550 ---
  Data developments and ticketing: The Agency will continue to foster develop-

--- Document Chunk 1551 ---
ments in the field of Linked data, as well as development under the TAP T si. The 

--- Document Chunk 1552 ---
Agency will continue its work on databases and registers optimisation. 

--- Document Chunk 1553 ---
  Communication and dissemination: The Agency will increase communicating 

--- Document Chunk 1554 ---
and disseminating relevant information and knowledge to its stakeholders, as well 

--- Document Chunk 1555 ---
as organising events and showcase the interesting projects and developments 

--- Document Chunk 1556 ---
within the rail sector. 

--- Document Chunk 1557 ---
  International Relations: The Agency will continue promoting Eu and interna -

--- Document Chunk 1558 ---
tional railway legislation and standards, as well as facilitating rail links in specific ge-

--- Document Chunk 1559 ---
ographical areas of interest to the European Commission, in particular to improve 

--- Document Chunk 1560 ---
safety and cross-border interoperability. 

--- Document Chunk 1561 ---
  Good governance: The Agency will strive for governance excellence and effi -

--- Document Chunk 1562 ---
ciency in all of its activities and will continue its efforts for improving budget exe -

--- Document Chunk 1563 ---
cution rates and overall compliance and performance.

--- Document Chunk 1564 ---
To best illustrate the alignment between sPd 2023 and sAP 2023-2027, the indicators and 

--- Document Chunk 1565 ---
targets which contribute to the strengthening Action Plan are indicated with a ticked box 

--- Document Chunk 1566 ---
in the annual tables hereinbelow. Moreover, the number of FTEs linked to sAP 2023-2027 

--- Document Chunk 1567 ---
is also highlighted in a separate column.

--- Document Chunk 1580 ---

--- Document Chunk 1584 ---

--- Document Chunk 1585 ---

--- Document Chunk 3687 ---
The following general principles guide the application of the legal framework concerning 

--- Document Chunk 3688 ---
the Agency staff:

--- Document Chunk 3689 ---
a.)  The core of the Agency staff consists of Temporary Agents. All Temporary Agent 

--- Document Chunk 3690 ---
positions have been identified as long-term positions. due to the budgetary and 

--- Document Chunk 3691 ---
establishment plan constraints the Agency is obliged to also engage Contract 

--- Document Chunk 3692 ---
Agents in order to fulfil its mission;

--- Document Chunk 3693 ---
b.)  Temporary and Contract Agents are treated equivalently as far as possible.

--- Document Chunk 3694 ---
in addition, it should be noted the Agency does not employ officials. however, there are 

--- Document Chunk 3695 ---
cases where Eu officials have been engaged following an external selection procedure 

--- Document Chunk 3696 ---
and have therefore acquired the status of Temporary Agent in the Agency (whilst remain-

--- Document Chunk 3697 ---
ing an official on unpaid leave in their institution of origin).

--- Document Chunk 3698 ---
i -  Selection and engagement procedures:

--- Document Chunk 3699 ---
The procedure for selection and engagement of Temporary Agents and Contract Agents 

--- Document Chunk 3700 ---
is based on Articles 27-34 of the staff Regulations  and Articles 12-15 and 82-84 of the 

--- Document Chunk 3701 ---
Conditions of Employment of o ther servants of the European Communities (CEos) , the 

--- Document Chunk 3702 ---
related implementing Rules on the engagement and use of Temporary Agents and Con -

--- Document Chunk 3703 ---
tract Agents, the Financial Regulation (European Commission’s Framework and that of the 

--- Document Chunk 3704 ---
Agency), the Code of good Administrative Behaviour and the data protection rules.

--- Document Chunk 3705 ---
The Agency also makes use of the EPso CAsT lists accessible to Agencies for the engage-

--- Document Chunk 3706 ---
ment of Contract Agents. Because of the Agreement on the European Economic Area 

--- Document Chunk 3707 ---
nationals of norway, iceland and Liechtenstein are eligible for working for the Agency.

--- Document Chunk 3708 ---
(50) Decision	n°204	of	the	Management	Board	of	the	European	Union	Agency	for	Railways	on	middle	management	staff

--- Document Chunk 3709 ---
(51) Decision	n°203	of	the	Management	Board	of	the	European	Union	Agency	for	Railways	on	types	of	post	and	post	

--- Document Chunk 3710 ---
titles	in	ERA

--- Document Chunk 3713 ---
The selection procedures for the engagement of Temporary Agents are carried out in ac -

--- Document Chunk 3714 ---
cordance with decision n° 121 of the Administrative Board of the European Railway Agen-

--- Document Chunk 3715 ---
cy laying down the general implementing provisions on the procedure governing the 

--- Document Chunk 3716 ---
engagement and use of temporary staff under Article 2(f ) of the CEos. 

--- Document Chunk 3717 ---
depending on the function and the level of tasks and within the limits authorised by the 

--- Document Chunk 3718 ---
establishment plan of the Agency, Temporary Agents are engaged at the following entry 

--- Document Chunk 3719 ---
grades:

--- Document Chunk 3720 ---
  AsT 1 to AsT 4 for the function group AsT

--- Document Chunk 3721 ---
  Ad 5 to Ad8 for the function group Ad

--- Document Chunk 3722 ---
For managerial posts or highly specialised posts, the Agency can engage Temporary 

--- Document Chunk 3723 ---
Agents at grades Ad 9 and Ad10 or at grade Ad12 for heads of department. 

--- Document Chunk 3724 ---
The duration of contracts for Temporary Agents is governed by d ecision n° ERA-Ed -

--- Document Chunk 3725 ---
dEC-1109-2015. staff holding a long-term post are normally offered an initial contract with 

--- Document Chunk 3726 ---
a duration of four years with the possibility of renewal. The standard practice for a first re-

--- Document Chunk 3727 ---
newal is normally for a two-year period and any further renewal is for an indefinite period. 

--- Document Chunk 3728 ---
For staff on short-term employment, the duration of the contract depends on the dura -

--- Document Chunk 3729 ---
tion of the tasks to be carried out. At ERA, the duration of those contracts is predominantly 

--- Document Chunk 3730 ---
related to the availability and duration of grants, or to a specific time determined project. 

--- Document Chunk 3731 ---
in very rare cases it is to cover long-term absences.

--- Document Chunk 3732 ---
The Agency is launching the following types of calls, published on ERA website’s Recruit-

--- Document Chunk 3733 ---
ment portal:

--- Document Chunk 3742 ---
ii -  Temporary agents

--- Document Chunk 3743 ---
The ERA Regulation 2016/796 which entered into force in 2016 makes no distinction be -

--- Document Chunk 3744 ---
tween posts for long- term and short-term employment. still a post can, in accordance 

--- Document Chunk 3745 ---
with Article 16 of decision n° 121, be defined to be for short-term employment when it 

--- Document Chunk 3746 ---
involves tasks of a limited duration.

--- Document Chunk 3747 ---
The decision to renew contracts of employment of Temporary Agents occupying a long-

--- Document Chunk 3748 ---
term post is taken by the Executive director based on two considerations: the continuity 

--- Document Chunk 3749 ---
of the post and the competences and performances of the jobholder, in accordance with 

--- Document Chunk 3750 ---
decision n° ERA-Ed -dEC-678-2013 and the Procedure PR o_sTA_01 on the “renewal and 

--- Document Chunk 3751 ---
non-renewal of contracts of employment before the expiry date” .

--- Document Chunk 3752 ---
if a TA or former TA is awarded a second contract of employment in the same function 

--- Document Chunk 3753 ---
group, this contract shall be considered as a renewal in the sense of Article 8 of the CEos if 

--- Document Chunk 3754 ---
the period between the end of the first contract and the starting date of the new contract 

--- Document Chunk 3755 ---
is less than 6 months. if the period between the two contracts of employment is 6 months 

--- Document Chunk 3756 ---
or more or if the new contract is in a different function group, the second contract of em-

--- Document Chunk 3757 ---
ployment shall be considered a new contract of employment.

--- Document Chunk 3758 ---
huMAn REsouRCEs 2023-2025 – Qu ALiTATiVE | 83

--- Document Chunk 3759 ---
iii -  Contract agents

--- Document Chunk 3760 ---
The selection procedures for the engagement of Contract Agents are carried out in ac -

--- Document Chunk 3761 ---
cordance with decision n° 210 of the Management Board of the European union Agency 

--- Document Chunk 3762 ---
on the general provisions for implementing Article 79(2) of the CEos, governing the con-

--- Document Chunk 3763 ---
ditions of employment of contract staff employed under the terms of Article 3a thereof. 

--- Document Chunk 3764 ---
in accordance with Article 85 of the CEos, contract staff can be engaged for a fixed pe -

--- Document Chunk 3765 ---
riod of at least three months and not more than five years. Contract Agents are engaged 

--- Document Chunk 3766 ---
for their specific competence in different areas of administration (finance, hR, iT, logistics, 

--- Document Chunk 3767 ---
legal, audit, quality management), in the railway domain or to perform manual or admin -

--- Document Chunk 3768 ---
istrative tasks. 

--- Document Chunk 3769 ---
This type of contract is usually used to meet specific needs such as:

--- Document Chunk 3770 ---
  Administrative tasks;

--- Document Chunk 3771 ---
  Coping with temporary peaks in workloads;

--- Document Chunk 3772 ---
  Launching projects or new activities for which long-term commitment in 

--- Document Chunk 3773 ---
terms of staffing is unclear;

--- Document Chunk 3774 ---
  Replacing staff on long-term absences such as maternity leave, long-term sick 

--- Document Chunk 3775 ---
leave or unpaid leave;

--- Document Chunk 3776 ---
however, increasingly ERA has also engaged Contract Agents for other (long-term) tasks, 

--- Document Chunk 3777 ---
such as:

--- Document Chunk 3778 ---
  Administrative and Logistician support Agents

--- Document Chunk 3779 ---
  Assistants

--- Document Chunk 3780 ---
  Project officers

--- Document Chunk 3781 ---
iv -  Seconded National Experts(52)

--- Document Chunk 3782 ---
seconded national Experts (snEs) are staff employed by a national, regional or local pub-

--- Document Chunk 3783 ---
lic administration or a public intergovernmental organisation who are seconded to the 

--- Document Chunk 3784 ---
Agency so that it can use their expertise in a particular field. snEs are seconded from 

--- Document Chunk 3785 ---
their national employer to the Agency’s operational units on the basis of their specific 

--- Document Chunk 3786 ---
competency and technical expertise in the railway domain, based on decision n° 173 of 

--- Document Chunk 3787 ---
the Management Board of the European union Agency for Railways laying down rules 

--- Document Chunk 3788 ---
on the secondment to the Agency of seconded national experts and national experts in 

--- Document Chunk 3789 ---
professional training.

--- Document Chunk 3790 ---
A possibility to mandate ‘cost-free’ snEs also exists, where the Agency does not pay any 

--- Document Chunk 3791 ---
allowances or cover any of the expenses related to the performance of their duties during 

--- Document Chunk 3792 ---
their secondment, although the Agency does not deploy such snEs at the moment. 

--- Document Chunk 3793 ---
snEs assist the Agency staff and cannot perform (middle) management duties. The initial 

--- Document Chunk 3794 ---
period of secondment may not be less than six months or more than two years. it may be 

--- Document Chunk 3795 ---
renewed once or more up to a total period not exceeding four years. Exceptionally, the 

--- Document Chunk 3796 ---
Agency’s Executive director may authorise one more extension of the secondment for 

--- Document Chunk 3797 ---
the maximum duration of one year at the end of the four-year period. Each secondment 

--- Document Chunk 3798 ---
and extension are subject to an exchange of letters. An snE may be seconded once again 

--- Document Chunk 3799 ---
provided that the conditions of secondment still exist and a period of at least six years has 

--- Document Chunk 3800 ---
elapsed between the end of the previous secondment and the new secondment unless 

--- Document Chunk 3801 ---
the previous secondments lasted for less than four years.

--- Document Chunk 3802 ---
(52)	 SNEs	are	not	employed	by	the	Agency

--- Document Chunk 3803 ---
84 | singLE PR ogRAMMing  doCuMEnT 2023-2025

Mobility policy

--- Document Chunk 3926 ---
Mobility within the Agency

--- Document Chunk 3927 ---
decision n° 121 of the Administrative Board of the European Railway Agency laying down 

--- Document Chunk 3928 ---
the general implementing provisions on the procedure governing the engagement and 

--- Document Chunk 3929 ---
use of temporary staff under Article 2(f ) of the CEos (adopted on 25.11.2016) and d e-

--- Document Chunk 3930 ---
cision n° 210 of the Management Board of the European union Agency on the general 

--- Document Chunk 3931 ---
provisions for implementing Article 79(2) of the CEos, governing the conditions of em -

--- Document Chunk 3932 ---
ployment of contract staff employed under the terms of Article 3a thereof enshrine the 

--- Document Chunk 3933 ---
scenarios for internal mobility for TA 2(f ) and CA. 

--- Document Chunk 3934 ---
The Agency considers internal mobility when vacancies arise, but due to the very specific, 

--- Document Chunk 3935 ---
technical competences of a big part of the staff, internal mobility remains limited.

--- Document Chunk 3936 ---
Furthermore, members of the Agency staff can apply for vacant posts within the Agency 

--- Document Chunk 3937 ---
advertised externally. A supplementary agreement in accordance with Article 10 of the 

--- Document Chunk 3938 ---
CEos will be concluded as required if existing staff get a new job.

--- Document Chunk 3939 ---
Mobility between Union Agencies

--- Document Chunk 3940 ---
The implementing rules on the engagement and use of Temporary Agents 2(f ) and Con-

--- Document Chunk 3941 ---
tract Agents define the scope of mobility between Eu Agencies. A very limited number 

--- Document Chunk 3942 ---
of the support staff who have left the Agency in previous years have accepted TA/CA 

--- Document Chunk 3943 ---
positions in other Agencies. 

--- Document Chunk 3944 ---
increasingly staff members who took up long-term Temporary Agent positions at the 

--- Document Chunk 3945 ---
Agency come from other Eu Agencies.

--- Document Chunk 3946 ---
Mobility between the agencies and the institutions

--- Document Chunk 3947 ---
some posts are filled following an external selection procedure by staff coming from other 

--- Document Chunk 3948 ---
European institutions (in particular the Commission), although the number remains small.

--- Document Chunk 4078 ---
Annex Vi. Environment 

--- Document Chunk 4079 ---
management

--- Document Chunk 4080 ---
Executive summary

--- Document Chunk 4081 ---
The revised sPd guidelines( 60) require Agencies to compile and formalise their Environ -

--- Document Chunk 4082 ---
ment management policy. To achieve this ambition, the first Environment management 

--- Document Chunk 4083 ---
annex was drafted in which ERA  summarised its commitment to higher policy 

--- Document Chunk 4084 ---
goals, the measures already in place, as well as the potential future environment 

--- Document Chunk 4085 ---
management initiatives and actions, taking in consideration the responsibilities of the 

--- Document Chunk 4086 ---
Agency as a public administration body, while keeping in mind the impact of environ -

--- Document Chunk 4087 ---
mental initiatives on the Agency’s limited human and financial resources. d espite these 

--- Document Chunk 4088 ---
limitations, the Agency is a socially and environmentally responsible organisation which 

--- Document Chunk 4089 ---
pursues, whenever possible, the adoption and related implementation of environmental 

--- Document Chunk 4090 ---
measures and initiatives that can be achieved with the available means.

--- Document Chunk 4091 ---
The Agency is committed to promote a culture of sustainability acting in a re -

--- Document Chunk 4092 ---
sponsible and sustainable manner  – see point 9 of the European union Agency for 

--- Document Chunk 4093 ---
Railways Policy(61). Concern for the environment and promoting a broader sustainability 

--- Document Chunk 4094 ---
agenda are integral to ERA’s professional activities and the management of the organisa -

--- Document Chunk 4095 ---
tion. in addition, the Agency is committed to urgently respond, within the boundaries 

--- Document Chunk 4096 ---
of its mandate and capacity, to the ongoing energy crisis.

--- Document Chunk 4097 ---
The Agency’s aim is to follow and to promote good sustainability practice, to reduce the 

--- Document Chunk 4098 ---
environmental impacts of its activities and to help its stakeholders to do the same. The 

--- Document Chunk 4099 ---
Agency’s existing environment principles(62) are covered under the following broader top-

--- Document Chunk 4100 ---
ics:

--- Document Chunk 4101 ---
green building(63) Climate protection Environmental preferable purchasing

--- Document Chunk 4102 ---
Transportation waste reduction and recycling sustainable resource management

--- Document Chunk 4103 ---
ERA’s wider work in the railway sector, including its authority and policy contribution to 

--- Document Chunk 4104 ---
a fully-fledged functioning Single European Railway Area , is covered under the 

--- Document Chunk 4105 ---
Annual work Programme, in particular strategic statement 2( 64) and the specific project 

--- Document Chunk 4106 ---
designated to “green agenda” (ERA1234).

--- Document Chunk 4107 ---
in addition to the broader policy context related to the green deal, the Agency pays atten-

--- Document Chunk 4108 ---
tion to the environmental impact of its day-to-day operations (i.e. to its building, staff, 

--- Document Chunk 4109 ---
management, administration, and functioning).

--- Document Chunk 4110 ---
ERA in the broader policy context related to environment

--- Document Chunk 4111 ---
As an Agency of the European union, ERA pledges to the Commission’s European 

--- Document Chunk 4112 ---
Green Deal(65) initiative. Consequently, ERA commits to deliver its part of the deal to 

--- Document Chunk 4113 ---
make the Eu’s climate, energy, transport and taxation policies fit for reducing net green -

--- Document Chunk 4114 ---
(60) Communication	C(2020)	2297	final	of	20.4.2020	on	the	strengthening	of	the	governance	of	Union	Bodies	under	

--- Document Chunk 4115 ---
Article	70	of	the	Financial	Regulation	2018/1046	and	on	the	guidelines	for	the	SPD	and	the	CAAR

--- Document Chunk 4116 ---

--- Document Chunk 4125 ---
house gas emissions by at least 55% by 2030, compared to 1990 levels – as defined in the 

--- Document Chunk 4126 ---
Eu Climate Target Plan 2030(66).

--- Document Chunk 4127 ---
since the publication of the Communication from the Commission on the European 

--- Document Chunk 4128 ---
green deal(67) in december 2019, ERA has strengthened its activities aiming at promoting 

--- Document Chunk 4129 ---
the role of the railways in the decarbonation of the European transport sector. To make the 

--- Document Chunk 4130 ---
European union the first carbon neutral region in the world by 2050, lowering the trans -

--- Document Chunk 4131 ---
port emissions is crucial. Between 1990 and 2019, the transport emissions have gradually 

--- Document Chunk 4132 ---
increased and reached 25% of the total greenhouse gas emissions of the Eu. The transport 

--- Document Chunk 4133 ---
sector is the second sector only to the energy sector in terms of emission.

--- Document Chunk 4134 ---
however, looking at the same period, the emissions of the railway sector have gradually 

--- Document Chunk 4135 ---
decreased and nowadays represent less than 0.5% of the transport-related emissions. i n 

--- Document Chunk 4136 ---
addition, railways are also the mode of transport with the lowest external costs (external -

--- Document Chunk 4137 ---
ities). 

--- Document Chunk 4138 ---
ERA has a central role in fostering interoperability and safety of the rail transport which 

--- Document Chunk 4139 ---
should eventually make it more attractive, more efficient and thereby increase the modal 

--- Document Chunk 4140 ---
share of the railways, resulting the greenhouse gas emissions of Europe’s transport sector, 

--- Document Chunk 4141 ---
in line with the objectives of the EC green deal:

--- Document Chunk 4142 ---
Figure 1 – Sustainable mobility targets (Source: EC)

reduction

--- Document Chunk 4298 ---
Environmental impacts of ERA activities

--- Document Chunk 4299 ---
ERA’s administrative operations related to its building(s) have direct and indirect impacts 

--- Document Chunk 4300 ---
on the environment. ERA’s impact on the environment falls under the following categories:

--- Document Chunk 4301 ---
1. use of electricity, including for heating and cooling, water, paper and 

--- Document Chunk 4302 ---
stationery

--- Document Chunk 4303 ---
2. generation of waste and Co2 emissions (including by travelling / com-

--- Document Chunk 4304 ---
muting)

--- Document Chunk 4305 ---
3. Land use with regards to biodiversity(70)

--- Document Chunk 4306 ---
ERA pays attention to limiting the use of resources, taking the energy crisis into account, 

--- Document Chunk 4307 ---
and minimising negative impacts on the environment.

--- Document Chunk 4308 ---
The recent geopolitical developments make the environmental – and in particular ener -

--- Document Chunk 4309 ---
gy-related issues – more visible than ever before.

--- Document Chunk 4310 ---
Accountability ceiling of ERA

--- Document Chunk 4311 ---
ERA is committed to do the utmost to advance its environment management and neutral-

--- Document Chunk 4312 ---
ise its impact on the environment. nevertheless, it needs to be noted that due to outside 

--- Document Chunk 4313 ---
factors ERA’s leverage may be limited regarding some proposed environment actions.

--- Document Chunk 4314 ---
Current ERA headquarters building was put at the disposal of ERA by Valenciennes Métro-

--- Document Chunk 4315 ---
pole through a rental contract. o ther buildings (meeting rooms in Lille, parking) used by 

--- Document Chunk 4316 ---
ERA are rented in office buildings and parking lots, where the environment management 

--- Document Chunk 4317 ---
responsibilities and tasks lie with the property owner or manager. i n the context of the 

--- Document Chunk 4318 ---
Covid-19 pandemic, the Agency has re-assessed its approach to meetings with stakehold-

--- Document Chunk 4319 ---
ers and has limited the use of office spaces in Lille, as well as the missions of ERA staff and 

--- Document Chunk 4320 ---
externals to Lille headquarters. A large number of the Agency’s meetings have been held 

--- Document Chunk 4321 ---
in remote mode, thus reducing the carbon footprint.

--- Document Chunk 4322 ---
Moreover, ERA’s new headquarters building project has a key focus on environmental con-

--- Document Chunk 4323 ---
siderations when setting up specifications and during negotiations.  The new building 

--- Document Chunk 4324 ---
project complies with the EMAs/hQE recommendations.

--- Document Chunk 4325 ---
it has to be noted that the railway link with the adjacent Belgian city of Mons is missing for 

--- Document Chunk 4326 ---
decades, with no rail service on the section between Valenciennes and the Franco-Belgian 

--- Document Chunk 4327 ---
border. despite recent plans brought back the hope for re-establishing the connection, as 

--- Document Chunk 4328 ---
of today this condition leaves no feasible public transportation option for the significant 

--- Document Chunk 4329 ---
proportion of ERA staff living in Belgium. ERA remains a vocal advocate of recommencing 

--- Document Chunk 4330 ---
cross-border railway operations as defined in its strategic statement 1(71), with a particular 

--- Document Chunk 4331 ---
focus on this particular one. nevertheless as of today, carbon footprint related to staff  

--- Document Chunk 4332 ---
commuting from Belgium to France needs to be mitigated with less desirable alternative 

--- Document Chunk 4333 ---
solutions, such as carpooling.

--- Document Chunk 4334 ---

to	be	considered	for	significant	improvement	of	its	biodiversity.

assets	can	be	reused	throughout	Europe”

Methodological notes:

--- Document Chunk 4399 ---
I. The actions listed in the sections below which require a budget envelope will start with a 

--- Document Chunk 4400 ---
budget estimate as a pre-requisite. Budget availability will be assessed for those actions 

--- Document Chunk 4401 ---
before proceeding with the implementation.

--- Document Chunk 4402 ---
II. Depending on the interest expressed for the volunteering group referred in part I, this group 

--- Document Chunk 4403 ---
can assist with other actions listed in parts A-I.

--- Document Chunk 4404 ---
III. While some of the units/teams are referred in the column of responsibilities by the nature 

--- Document Chunk 4405 ---
of their role in the organisation, the successful implementation of the strategy relies on the 

--- Document Chunk 4406 ---
ownership and involvement of all staff members.

--- Document Chunk 4407 ---
A�   Consumption of resources (energy & utilities) 

--- Document Chunk 4408 ---
ERA collects and analyses information related to the consumption of 

--- Document Chunk 4409 ---
electricity and water.

--- Document Chunk 4410 ---
A Pareto analysis of energy consumption will be conducted to pinpoint the critical points 

--- Document Chunk 4411 ---
to concentrate on and put efforts in first. Based on this information, ERA will identify any 

--- Document Chunk 4412 ---
possible action to decrease the consumption.

C�   Green public procurement(74) 

--- Document Chunk 4450 ---
ERA to further improve its procurement by implementing green public 

--- Document Chunk 4451 ---
procurement by the end of 2023. ERA to advance green public procurement 

--- Document Chunk 4452 ---
by promoting the use and order of “green office items” from the EC office 

--- Document Chunk 4453 ---
supplies’ catalogue.

--- Document Chunk 4454 ---
Calls for procurement tenders of relevant goods and services should include “Environmen-

--- Document Chunk 4455 ---
tal and social contribution” among the technical evaluation criteria (e.g. decommissioned 

--- Document Chunk 4456 ---
furniture disposal/re-use, recycling policy, donations). An “environmental impact state -

--- Document Chunk 4457 ---
ment” will be written in the initial proposal for procurement and specific, robust environ -

--- Document Chunk 4458 ---
mental criteria, and “environmental considerations” will be included in the calls for pro -

--- Document Chunk 4459 ---
curement tenders of relevant goods, and services include. Tenderers will have to comply 

--- Document Chunk 4460 ---
with these criteria and considerations to qualify for a contract. it is planned to become a 

--- Document Chunk 4461 ---
standard ERA practice to build environmental considerations into procurement for rele -

--- Document Chunk 4462 ---
vant goods and services.

--- Document Chunk 4465 ---
D�   Carbon footprint reduction and management of missions, 

--- Document Chunk 4466 ---
meetings and events 

--- Document Chunk 4467 ---
ERA will promote and utilise the Commission’s guidelines on organising 

--- Document Chunk 4468 ---
sustainable meetings and events. It will implement MIPS module of 

--- Document Chunk 4469 ---
Sysper to replace MiMa and will compile regular reports on travel-related 

--- Document Chunk 4470 ---
emissions starting from 2023. ERA will amend its travel policy to encourage 

--- Document Chunk 4471 ---
environmentally friendlier itineraries.

--- Document Chunk 4472 ---
ERA adheres to Commission’s guidelines on organising sustainable meetings and 

--- Document Chunk 4473 ---
events(75), and commits to promote the guidelines and incentivise to its staff to apply the 

--- Document Chunk 4474 ---
steps when organising meetings and events:

--- Document Chunk 4475 ---
  step 0: is a physical meeting/event necessary?

--- Document Chunk 4476 ---
  step 1: is the venue sustainable enough?

--- Document Chunk 4477 ---
  step 2: is the printed and promotional material sustainable?

--- Document Chunk 4478 ---
  step 3: Are the 3Rs applied? (Reduce, Recycle and Reuse)

--- Document Chunk 4479 ---
  step 4: is the catering sustainable?

--- Document Chunk 4480 ---
  step 5: Are the accommodation and transport environmentally friendly?

--- Document Chunk 4481 ---
  step 6: have social aspects been considered?

--- Document Chunk 4482 ---
  step 7: Are you sharing environmental awareness?

--- Document Chunk 4483 ---
The Agency could strengthen the recommendation for internal and external attendees 

--- Document Chunk 4484 ---
to select train transportation where convenient connections are available, or air travel op-

--- Document Chunk 4485 ---
tions with smaller carbon footprint (e.g. more direct flight routes, less connections). i n 

--- Document Chunk 4486 ---
addition, travel policy and related internal communications will repeatedly emphasise to 

--- Document Chunk 4487 ---
ERA staff that online meeting forms should be preferred and picked over travel intensive 

--- Document Chunk 4488 ---
face-to-face meetings whenever feasible and expedient. 

--- Document Chunk 4489 ---
E�   Further reduction of paper and stationery consumption 

--- Document Chunk 4490 ---
ERA will continue to fully digitise workflows. It will further reduce the 

--- Document Chunk 4491 ---
printouts of publications. In the limited cased of printers’ use, ERA will 

--- Document Chunk 4492 ---
maintain the use of eco-friendly / partially recycled A4 printing paper as 

--- Document Chunk 4493 ---
a default printing medium. It will introduce on-demand stationery supply 

--- Document Chunk 4494 ---
instead of stationery “welcome package” .

--- Document Chunk 4495 ---
ERA will advance further digitalisation of the Agency, including the replacement of pa -

--- Document Chunk 4496 ---
per-based processes with electronic workflows and other iT systems – in cooperation with 

--- Document Chunk 4497 ---
the Commission’s dg digiT – such as:

--- Document Chunk 4498 ---
  sysPER (full rollout)

--- Document Chunk 4499 ---
  Microsoft sharePoint and office 365: office solutions for paperless document cre -

--- Document Chunk 4500 ---
ation and storing (full rollout)

--- Document Chunk 4501 ---
  Ares: document management and archiving system

--- Document Chunk 4502 ---
ERA will continue to reduce the number of printed (paper-based) publications through 

--- Document Chunk 4503 ---
close management of the communication & publication plan. ERA will increase the use of 

--- Document Chunk 4504 ---
print on demand of its publications/materials and web publishing.

--- Document Chunk 4505 ---

--- Document Chunk 4506 ---
perless office. As part of it, instead of the usual stationery “welcome package” , office sup-

--- Document Chunk 4507 ---
plies will continue to be stored in a designated office and colleagues will be invited to 

--- Document Chunk 4508 ---
collect strictly what they need – on demand.

F�   Waste generation reduction, sorting and recycling 

--- Document Chunk 4513 ---
ERA will maintain – or if possible, improve – the selective recycling and 

--- Document Chunk 4514 ---
waste collection arrangements in its current building, as well as in the 

--- Document Chunk 4515 ---
new building. ERA will order office supplies and merchandise on an on-

--- Document Chunk 4516 ---
demand basis only, with preference to sustainable/recycled/eco-friendly 

--- Document Chunk 4517 ---
distributable merchandise.

--- Document Chunk 4518 ---
ERA will make sure that selective waste collection remains widely available in offices and 

--- Document Chunk 4519 ---
common areas of the current building and undertakes to provide for the same in the new 

--- Document Chunk 4520 ---
building. in the form of internal communication, ERA will raise awareness among its staff  

--- Document Chunk 4521 ---
about these recycling arrangements.

--- Document Chunk 4522 ---
Moreover, ERA has a partner to recycle decommissioned iT equipment.

--- Document Chunk 4647 ---

--- Document Chunk 4648 ---
longer the required conditions to accommodate staff and activities related to the Agen -

--- Document Chunk 4649 ---
cy’s role as railways’ Authority. Therefore, the Agency has re-allocated the majority of staff  

--- Document Chunk 4650 ---
members in double office spaces as a short-term solution. Another short-medium term 

--- Document Chunk 4651 ---
solution is the implementation of teleworking up to the limit set by the Management 

--- Document Chunk 4652 ---
Board decision on Teleworking.

--- Document Chunk 4653 ---
in parallel, as part of a long-term solution, the Agency and Valenciennes Métropole have 

--- Document Chunk 4654 ---
started defining the requirements for a new building to accommodate ERA activities after 

--- Document Chunk 4655 ---
2027 by means of a study composed of different phases. in 2018, the Phase i of the study 

--- Document Chunk 4656 ---
confirmed that the current ERA hQ cannot accommodate all requirements related to the 

--- Document Chunk 4657 ---
Agency activities and growth.

--- Document Chunk 4658 ---
in 2019 and 2020, the Agency has managed to complete the Phases 2 and 4 of the tech -

--- Document Chunk 4659 ---
nical and functional study resulting in the approval of the technical specifications that will 

--- Document Chunk 4660 ---
be used as the base for the selection of architects in the Phase 3 of the study.

--- Document Chunk 4661 ---
Taking into account the experience gained during the pandemic with large-scale tele -

--- Document Chunk 4662 ---
working and new ways of working, the building capacity was revised, and the technical 

--- Document Chunk 4663 ---
project adapted.

--- Document Chunk 4664 ---
The main objective for the Agency during 2021 was to prepare the technical and financial 

--- Document Chunk 4665 ---
dossier to be formally addressed to the Eu Budgetary Authority for the financing of a new 

--- Document Chunk 4666 ---
building.

--- Document Chunk 4667 ---
in 2022, following the approval of the project, it is foreseen that Valenciennes Métropole 

--- Document Chunk 4668 ---
will launch a “Concours” (Contest / CFT) for the selection of the Architect as part of the 

--- Document Chunk 4669 ---
Phase 3 of the Project.

Annex Viii. Privileges and immunities

--- Document Chunk 4676 ---
The Management Board approved the proposed headquarters (or seat) Agreement between the Agency and the host Member state without objections or negative votes in August 2018.

--- Document Chunk 4677 ---
(83) The seat Agreement between the French government and the Agency has been presented as draft legislation to the French national Assembly on 7 July 2021(84) and has been adopted 

--- Document Chunk 4678 ---
and promulgated on 31 January 2022. The final text of the seat Agreement can be found here(85). The following table presents the privileges granted to the Agency’s staff:(86)

Annex iX. Evaluations

--- Document Chunk 4769 ---
The Agency has a system in place to monitor its performance and formalise an evaluation 

--- Document Chunk 4770 ---
of the results achieved in the year into the SPD dashboard, as an ongoing tool, as well 

--- Document Chunk 4771 ---
as through the Consolidated Annual Activity Report , which focuses on the achieve -

--- Document Chunk 4772 ---
ments of indicators and targets set out in the sPd.

--- Document Chunk 4773 ---
The following instruments are used for collecting the data and for triggering actions:

--- Document Chunk 4774 ---
  Work progress reports, filled in by projects and service managers reporting the 

--- Document Chunk 4775 ---
status of projects and services against the relevant plans, budget and human re -

--- Document Chunk 4776 ---
sources allocation, including sPd targets.

--- Document Chunk 4777 ---
  Budget execution monitoring, a continuous activity based on a daily automat-

--- Document Chunk 4778 ---
ed report fed with suMMA data, displaying the level of appropriations, commit -

--- Document Chunk 4779 ---
ments and payments to date for each budget line and for each project/service

--- Document Chunk 4780 ---
  Monthly budget review meetings with the Management Team to analyse the 

--- Document Chunk 4781 ---
data from the budget execution monitoring and take timely decisions for deploy-

--- Document Chunk 4782 ---
ing / redeploying the resources. The redeployment of resources is brought to the 

--- Document Chunk 4783 ---
attention of the Management Board for information if the transfers are within one 

--- Document Chunk 4784 ---
title or between titles but below the 10% threshold or for decision if the transfers 

--- Document Chunk 4785 ---
are between titles and above the 10% threshold.

--- Document Chunk 4786 ---
  IMS internal audits, part of the internal monitoring programme aimed at verify -

--- Document Chunk 4787 ---
ing that processes, projects, services and products comply with internal and exter-

--- Document Chunk 4788 ---
nal requirements, including.

--- Document Chunk 4789 ---
  IAS audits

--- Document Chunk 4790 ---
  ECA audits

--- Document Chunk 4791 ---
  Non-Conformity register, where deviations from the relevant rules and provi -

--- Document Chunk 4792 ---
sions are recorded 

--- Document Chunk 4793 ---
All the sources listed above allow the Agency governance bodies, namely the Manage -

--- Document Chunk 4794 ---
ment Team and the Management Board to monitor continuously the functioning of the 

--- Document Chunk 4795 ---
Agency. in order to allow this, the Agency has developed a performance dashboard 

--- Document Chunk 4796 ---
which is turning the data into meaningful information.

Annexes

--- Document Chunk 4863 ---
Terminology(87)

--- Document Chunk 4864 ---
The following terms are used in the sPd – in accordance with the Commission guideline 

--- Document Chunk 4865 ---
on evaluation:

--- Document Chunk 4866 ---
Strategic Statement(88) is a coherent area of action with objectives and resources. i t is 

--- Document Chunk 4867 ---
the basic building block for the structure of the annual work Programme, distinguishing 

--- Document Chunk 4868 ---
between operational activities – directly related to the mission and core tasks of the agen-

--- Document Chunk 4869 ---
cy, and horizontal/ cross-cutting activities – carried out to support operational activities 

--- Document Chunk 4870 ---
and staff.

--- Document Chunk 4871 ---
Objective describes what the agency wants to achieve either in the short or long term.

--- Document Chunk 4872 ---
Indicator is a characteristic or attribute that is measured regularly in order to assess to 

--- Document Chunk 4873 ---
what extent an objective has been met.

--- Document Chunk 4874 ---
Baseline is the point of reference against which achievement or progress towards objec-

--- Document Chunk 4875 ---
tives is measured.

--- Document Chunk 4876 ---
Milestone is an intermediate target set, expressed in quantitative or qualitative terms, 

--- Document Chunk 4877 ---
measuring progress towards the achievement of long-term objectives.

--- Document Chunk 4878 ---
Target is the ultimate desired situation, quantified and timed.

--- Document Chunk 4879 ---
Inputs are the human and financial resources used and the time required to produce 

--- Document Chunk 4880 ---
outputs.

--- Document Chunk 4881 ---
Actions are the work carried out over a certain period of time, consuming resources and 

--- Document Chunk 4882 ---
producing outputs in accordance with the objectives set.

--- Document Chunk 4883 ---
Outputs are what is directly produced or supplied through the agency intervention. They 

--- Document Chunk 4884 ---
often relate to the expected deliverables of the intervention and are identified based on 

--- Document Chunk 4885 ---
its operational objectives.

--- Document Chunk 4886 ---
Outcome is the envisaged medium to long term effects of a programme or policy out -

--- Document Chunk 4887 ---
put. while its results are not easily foreseeable and might not be entirely in the sphere of 

--- Document Chunk 4888 ---
control of the Agency, the outcome represents an intermediate medium-term step be -

--- Document Chunk 4889 ---
tween the agency’ outputs and longer-term societal impacts. The Agency has structured 

--- Document Chunk 4890 ---
its multiannual work programme according to desired outcomes to ensure all of its out -

--- Document Chunk 4891 ---
puts will contribute positively to its vision & ambition.

--- Document Chunk 4892 ---
Results are the direct effects of intervention(s) on the target groups.

--- Document Chunk 4893 ---
Impacts are the indirect or long-term effects of an intervention on the Eu or global socie-

--- Document Chunk 4894 ---
ty that are, at least partly, expected to be influenced by agency’s interventions.

--- Document Chunk 4899 ---
Annex X. strategy for 

--- Document Chunk 4900 ---
the organisational 

--- Document Chunk 4901 ---
management and 

--- Document Chunk 4902 ---
internal control 

--- Document Chunk 4903 ---
systems

--- Document Chunk 4904 ---
The strategy gives an overview on how the internal control system is organised and is 

--- Document Chunk 4905 ---
contributing to the mitigation of the risks to the achievement of Agency’s objectives to 

--- Document Chunk 4906 ---
acceptable levels.

--- Document Chunk 4907 ---
The Agency is operating based on a management system designed to provide reasona -

--- Document Chunk 4908 ---
ble assurance regarding the achievement of the five internal control objectives derived 

--- Document Chunk 4909 ---
from the Agency’s Financial regulation as well as ensuring continuous improvement and 

--- Document Chunk 4910 ---
the need to implement a flexible and effective governance. The management system is 

--- Document Chunk 4911 ---
implemented through four high-level components (i) strategic, (ii) Core, (iii) support and 

--- Document Chunk 4912 ---
(iv) Measurement and improvement. Each component is including all 17 principles of the 

--- Document Chunk 4913 ---
internal Control Framework (iCF). There is also a clear link with the internal components of 

--- Document Chunk 4914 ---
the iCF (i.e. control environment, risk assessment, control activities and monitoring). This 

--- Document Chunk 4915 ---
system is deployed further at the level of processes. 

--- Document Chunk 4916 ---
The roles and responsibilities for implementing the system are integrated as follows:

--- Document Chunk 4917 ---
The Management Board represents the Member states, and the institutional stakehold-

--- Document Chunk 4918 ---
ers has a strategic role on budgetary and planning matters. i t is overseeing the internal 

--- Document Chunk 4919 ---
controls and risk management of the Agency. it ensures that the Agency fulfils its mission 

--- Document Chunk 4920 ---
and performs the tasks assigned to it

--- Document Chunk 4921 ---
The Executive Director (ED) in its capacity of Authorising officer (Ao) and under the su-

--- Document Chunk 4922 ---
pervision of the Management Board is ultimately responsible for the management of the 

--- Document Chunk 4923 ---
internal control framework. The Ed sets the tone at the tope and puts in place structures 

--- Document Chunk 4924 ---
and processes to gain reasonable assurance that the system is operating effectively.

--- Document Chunk 4925 ---
The heads of units/department  in their capacity of/Authorising officer by delegation 

--- Document Chunk 4926 ---
(Aod) must ensure that the internal controls are efficient and effective in their area of re -

--- Document Chunk 4927 ---
sponsibility as per Ao delegation of powers. Both Ao and Aod in their capacity of process 

--- Document Chunk 4928 ---
owners are responsible for continuous improvement of the processes.

--- Document Chunk 4929 ---
The newly created function of manager in charge of Risk management and internal 

--- Document Chunk 4930 ---
control is fulfilled by a middle manager. i t oversees the monitoring the implementation 

--- Document Chunk 4931 ---
of the internal control arrangements and for complete and accurate reporting on the op-

--- Document Chunk 4932 ---
eration and effectiveness of the internal control framework. This function is also in charge 

--- Document Chunk 4933 ---
of facilitating the risk management process. 

--- Document Chunk 4934 ---
The accounting officer certifies the year-end accounts thus providing reasonable assur-

--- Document Chunk 4935 ---
ance that the accounts present a true and fair view of the financial situation of the Agency. 

--- Document Chunk 4936 ---
All staff should ensure at their own level of competency that their activities comply with 

--- Document Chunk 4937 ---
rules and regulations and report any deficiency.

--- Document Chunk 4938 ---
The delegations of powers for executing the budget are detailed in internal procedures. 

--- Document Chunk 4939 ---
The implementation of the budget is done via projects and services which is reflected in 

--- Document Chunk 4940 ---
